  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_28d03294-a886-4b53-afe9-8e8d39ca8d67'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();

      initializeSiwa();
    }

  <span id="freeText3993404297855846110" style="display:none"><strong>Tahereh Mafi's <em>New York Times</em> bestselling Shatter Me series is perfect for fans who crave action-packed young adult novels like Veronica Roth’s <em>Divergent</em>, Suzanne Collins’s <em>The Hunger Games</em>, and Marie Lu’s <em>Legend</em>.</strong><br /><br />No one knows why Juliette's touch is fatal, but The Reestablishment has plans for her. Plans to use her as a weapon. But Juliette has plans of her own. After a lifetime without freedom, she's finally discovering a strength to fight for herself—and for a future with the one boy she thought she'd lost forever.<br /><br />Tahereh Mafi has created a captivating and original story that combines the best of dystopian and paranormal and was praised by <em>Publishers Weekly</em> as "a gripping read from an author who's not afraid to take risks." This collection includes the first three novels, <em>Shatter Me, Unravel Me, </em>and <em>Ignite Me</em>; and the two novellas in the series, <em>Destroy Me</em> and <em>Fracture Me</em>.<br /><br /><strong>And don’t miss <em>Defy Me</em></strong><strong>, the shocking fifth book in the Shatter Me series!</strong></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer974791970" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer10100554196910646942">This book series left me with a serious book hangover. I have never had a book hangover like this either. It was a serious bender that lead to the worst book hangover ever. You get so caught up in the story, so tied in with the characters, that when the final word are read and you shut the cover of the book all you can do is stare at the wall for a minute and think to yourself, "What do I do now?" <br/><br/>I strongly recommend this series for someone looking to be swept away. Tahereh sucks you into this </span>
  <span id="freeText10100554196910646942" style="display:none">This book series left me with a serious book hangover. I have never had a book hangover like this either. It was a serious bender that lead to the worst book hangover ever. You get so caught up in the story, so tied in with the characters, that when the final word are read and you shut the cover of the book all you can do is stare at the wall for a minute and think to yourself, "What do I do now?" <br /><br />I strongly recommend this series for someone looking to be swept away. Tahereh sucks you into this dystopian world and throws you through the emotional dry cycle. </span>

<div id="review_1059951167" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1059951167" />
    <a title="Anna Kis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33789901-anna-kis"><img alt="Anna Kis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1418709448p2/33789901.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1059951167?book_show_action=true">Sep 20, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anna Kis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anna Kis" href="/user/show/33789901-anna-kis">Anna Kis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33789901-anna-kis?shelf=faves">faves</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1059951167" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer362905620708492685">I picked up this book one day because I was bored, and I thought it would be a great filler-book, just a quick read that I wouldn't get attached to. I only had the first book, but I assumed that I wasn't going to be into it enough to spend more money on the series.<br/>I was so incredibly wrong.<br/>I started Shatter Me expecting a shitty novel with a weird writing style and a re-used plot, but what I got was a unique, interesting, and wonderful take on the popular dystopian genre. Instead of being bland </span>
  <span id="freeText362905620708492685" style="display:none">I picked up this book one day because I was bored, and I thought it would be a great filler-book, just a quick read that I wouldn't get attached to. I only had the first book, but I assumed that I wasn't going to be into it enough to spend more money on the series.<br />I was so incredibly wrong.<br />I started Shatter Me expecting a shitty novel with a weird writing style and a re-used plot, but what I got was a unique, interesting, and wonderful take on the popular dystopian genre. Instead of being bland and boring it was incredibly interesting, and despite being someone who prefers to stick to more traditional writing styles, I enjoyed the way the author wrote the book so, so much. <br />and so I read, then bought, the other two books in the series - I just couldn't live without them. (note: if you've read shatter Me, read Destroy Me before you continue with Unravel Me) the next two books were so incredibly amazing I read them both in a day - I couldn't put them down. They absorbed you into this messed up world, and I began to become so passionate about the characters.<br /> The writing is raw and all over the place - but that makes the book so much better, the characters so much more interesting. <br />well, now I'm just rambling. But I loved this series so much, and I recommend it because it is so so so amazing.<br />Read it.<br />Now.</span>
  <a data-text-id="362905620708492685" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1067142563" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1067142563" />
    <a title="Emily Florence" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15175074-emily-florence"><img alt="Emily Florence" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573038222p2/15175074.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1067142563?book_show_action=true">Sep 29, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily Florence" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily Florence" href="/user/show/15175074-emily-florence">Emily Florence</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1067142563" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9526293609739270889">First of all I absolutely have to mention… THE COVERS. Oh my eyes. They are so so so beautiful. Hats off to whoever designed these beauties. The books are worth buying just to have such gorgeousness on my bookshelf. *swoon*<br/><br/><br/>I remember when I first read Shatter Me I was intrigued by the idea but a little put of by Tahereh Mafi’s writing style. It was too much for me, too poetic and struck me as trying too hard and failing. It was distracting me from the story. Some of the lines had me stopping lik</span>
  <span id="freeText9526293609739270889" style="display:none">First of all I absolutely have to mention… THE COVERS. Oh my eyes. They are so so so beautiful. Hats off to whoever designed these beauties. The books are worth buying just to have such gorgeousness on my bookshelf. *swoon*<br /><br /><br />I remember when I first read Shatter Me I was intrigued by the idea but a little put of by Tahereh Mafi’s writing style. It was too much for me, too poetic and struck me as trying too hard and failing. It was distracting me from the story. Some of the lines had me stopping like really?! Why oh why? That makes no sense and is actually quite disturbing.<br /><br /><br />“My words wear no parachutes as they fall out of my mouth”<br /><br />“The sky is raining bricks right into my skull.”<br /><br />“My eyes break open. Two shattered windows filling my mouth with glass.”<br /><br />“He shifts and my eyes shatter into thousands of pieces that ricochet around the room, capturing a million snapshots, a million moments in time. Flickering images faded with age, frozen thoughts hovering precariously in dead space, a whirlwind of memories that slice through my soul.”<br /><br /><br />Ugh, Its like that all the way through, constantly. It really grates on my nerves. It’s just unneeded and quite frankly annoying.<br /><br />Despite this I pushed on through the book. I’d heard some good reviews that advised me to just get used to the writing style and keep going. So I did. Eventually you just sort of get used to the over use of metaphors that barely make sense.<br /><br />The world its set in isn’t too bad but it isn’t focused on enough, or else we missed it in-between the personifications of the sun and metaphors about breathing. Its a typical dystopia, world gone wrong little group of rebels out to save everything. Except this group of rebels all have magical powers.<br /><br /><br /><br />It’s very X-Men gone wrong. They keep saying they have some big plan but really they don’t seem to be doing much. From what I gathered there aren’t very many of them and they plan to attack someone or someplace in Sector 45 where they live and win (plausible), then they’re gonna somehow use this victory to save everyone across the entire country… (not plausible). It struck me as badly thought out.<br /><br />And Omega Point (rebels really cool little hideout) just seems to be used as a stage for Juliette and Adams relationship (if you can even call it that) drama. I mean come on! So much potential to make me fall in love and be dying to go to Omega Point and its just tarnished by stupid arguments. This at least is pointed out by the fantastic Kenji, who straight up lets them know that they are being dumb. (Kenji is fab btw).<br /><br />In the first book Juliette is annoying whiny and childish. I get that she’d been locked up for ages on her own so she was bound to be less than her best but ugh seriously, I just wanted someone to put her back in her cell.<br /><br />Adam has the personality of a potato. An especially bland potato. He is boring and dull and all he has going for him is his ridiculous insta-love for Juliette. I HATE INSTA-LOVE. They tried to play it off as childhood sweethearts but seriously she let someone cheat off her when she was nine and suddenly Adam thinks she’s gods gift. He treats her like some kind sweet innocent little flower that he needs to protect. She’s a kind person, that doesn’t make her an endangered species Adam, jeez. Juliette is tough under all her whining, anyone could see that. She needs to be pushed and challenged to wake up the real Juliette inside, not coddled.<br /><br />I get Juliette instant attraction to Adam, first person to be able to touch her her whole life? Shes gonna feel something. That something however is not love, if anything its lust and the first taste of friendship she’s ever had all mushed up. And that’s being generous to Mr Dull Potato Adam. The only redeeming quality to Adam is his love for is brother James. I do love it when YA shows some good sibling relationships.<br /><br />As for the other characters; James is adorable and funny, loved him. Kenji is fantastic, seriously fantastic. Id give him his own book. I want him as my new best friend, loved loved loved him. Castle was not so great although I did like his and Kenji’s relationship.<br /><br />Finally, Warner. My oh my oh my.<br /> What a character. I think hes responsible for at least 3 stars of my review. Without him I would not have been able to read on. He is amazing, fanastic, brilliant, perfect… AAAGH, there are no words for him…<br /><br />He is exactly what I needed Juliette needed. He brings out the best in her even when he’s not with her. And so by the end of the series Juliette becomes a kickass main character who knows what she wants, all thanks to my boyfriend Warner.<br /><br />The first two books are mediocre, 2 stars for Shatter Me and 3 for Unravel Me. Ignite me is by far the best of the triology, 4 stars. Destroy Me gets 3.5 and Fracture Me gets a measly 1.5 stars because Adam is just so BORING.<br /><br />Overall I give the series as a whole 3.5 stars. If you can power through the first book then well done! and keep going!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9526293609739270889" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7515832-jamie-therebelliousreader?shelf=my-book-boyfriend">my-book-boyfriend</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7515832-jamie-therebelliousreader?shelf=this-is-trash-and-so-am-i">this-is-trash-and-so-am-i</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2817017494" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6753613654316172637"><b>Shatter Me:</b><br/>Original rating: ★★☆☆☆ Read in 2012<br/>Rating after re-read: ★★☆☆☆ Read 5/11/19<br/><br/>Seven years later and this is still just as awful as I remembered. This first book is a hot, boiling ass mess and I will never understand the hype of it and why people tote it as the second coming. The writing is just above tolerable but the prose is laughably bad. Terrible, cheesy dialogue, a weak main character in Juliette and to top it off we get the bland bowl of oatmeal that is Adam Kent. *snores* Thank Go</span>
  <span id="freeText6753613654316172637" style="display:none"><b>Shatter Me:</b><br />Original rating: ★★☆☆☆ Read in 2012<br />Rating after re-read: ★★☆☆☆ Read 5/11/19<br /><br />Seven years later and this is still just as awful as I remembered. This first book is a hot, boiling ass mess and I will never understand the hype of it and why people tote it as the second coming. The writing is just above tolerable but the prose is laughably bad. Terrible, cheesy dialogue, a weak main character in Juliette and to top it off we get the bland bowl of oatmeal that is Adam Kent. *snores* Thank God for the love of my life Warner and my spirit animal Kenji because they made this book. Without them this would’ve been a one star read because I genuinely don’t like it. I will say that the next two books are leaps and bounds better but damn this first one is just a dumpster fire.<br /><br /><b>Destroy Me (1.5 Novella):</b><br />Original rating: ★★★★★ Read in 2013<br />Rating after re-read: ★★★★★ Read 5/11/19<br /><br />I still love this novella with all of my heart and soul. It’s heartbreaking and emotional. I hate seeing what Warner has gone through and what he still goes through with his father. It’s fascinating being inside of his head and seeing a human side to him after the first book. Warner is one of my all time favorite book boyfriends and I will always love this short story. He’s such a tortured soul and I cannot get enough of him and I think this was wonderfully done and is an important part to not only Warner’s character but the series overall.<br /><br /><b>Unravel Me:</b><br />Original rating: ★★★☆☆ Read in 2013<br />Rating after re-read: ★★★☆☆ Read 5/12/19<br /><br />The first 200 pages are incredibly slow and boring to get through but then Warner and his father show up and shake shit up and things finally get going. This has a lot of great action and I loved the ending but there’s so much wangst between Juliette and Adam that I just wanted to bash my head into the wall. Juliette is starting to come into her own here and while she is still incredibly whiny and passive, I can see the development and I think her absolute best moments were when she was interacting with Warner, Kenji and Castle. All three of them really brought out something different in her that I enjoyed.<br /><br /><b>Fracture Me (2.5 Novella):</b><br />Original rating: ★★★☆☆ Read in 2013<br />Rating after re-read: ★☆☆☆☆ Read 5/12/19<br /><br />LMAO. A boring novella about a boring bowl of oatmeal. Yawn. Doesn’t add anything of importance. Just solidifies my hatred for Adam.<br /><br /><b>Ignite Me:</b><br />Original rating: ★★★☆☆ Read in 2014<br />Rating after re-read: ★★★★☆ Read 5/13/19<br /><br />Okay, so this one surprised me the most out of this entire re-read of the series. I remember thinking that this last book was decent and I had enjoyed it enough but there was something about it this time around that I really liked. There’s a lot of character development in this and with the exception of one person (Adam, because of course it’s him) it’s very well done. It’s about Juliette tapping into her inner strength and finally becoming the person she should’ve been from the jump. Warner’s character development was honestly my favorite of the two of them because he has a lot more emotional growth and moments where we really get to see his character stripped down to it’s most basic level and it was wonderful. The two of them together bring out the best in each other without trying to change compromise who that person is as an individual and I appreciated. They grew on their own but together if that makes any sense and it makes their relationship feel very solid. This was a pretty good ending to the series but I can definitely see how Mafi left it open in the end to write more.<br /><br />Overall, this series is like candy. I re-read all of these in three days. They’re not all that good (minus the last one) but they’re addicting as hell. I’m looking forward to finally continuing on with the series and seeing where she takes the characters from here. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6753613654316172637" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText879660973995724329" style="display:none">First I would like to say that I'm writing this review for the whole Shatter Me series, and second that I never EVER write reviews... That being said here's my review of the shatter me series. <br /><br />	Breathtaking, wonderful, stunning.... I could use any of those words to describe this series but they would all be understatement. <br /><br />Mafi's writing is beyond refreshing and unique. It's something so hard to describe or even put into words, and I know that my review wont do it true justice.<br /><br />I found myself drowning in her words and not wanting to come up for air. I wanted the waves of her writing to crash over me and pull me further and further out. I'm pretty sure I held my breath the whole time I was reading this series (which might I add I finished in less than two days).<br /><br />Since finishing this series I have found myself comparing any book I have read or am reading to it. Never has a writer made me fall so in love with characters and made me feel like whatever happened to them was happening to me. Her characters will steal your heart and soul. Juliette will make you feel empowered and brave. Adam will make you remember what love feels like. Warner will show you everything you secretly want and OH BOY WILL YOU WANT IT, and Kenji will be the friend you've always wanted.<br /><br />I could go on for <s>days</s>... <s>weeks</s>... no years about this book. I would go so into detail and fine tooth comb and break down every chapter if I could, but I wont because I would never want to tarnish, or give out any details to someone who hasn't had the chance to read this masterpiece, because that's what this series is. It's the Mona Lisa of ya novels. A slight mysterious smile that you can't turn away from. It makes you want to scream out loud and kiss Tahereh's forehead and thank her for writing something so on point. so on point. <br /><br />I could seriously keep going, but I'll spare you the novel of a review I could write and leave you with this.....<br />	You know how you meet someone with such passion for what they do and all you can think is "wow, this person was born to do this" <b>well Tahereh Mafi was meant to be a writer, and I'm SO very thankful that she is! Thanks for the permanent goose bumps, tears, laughs, and never ending book hang over that you have rewarded me with.I am forever in your debt. </b><br /><br />Read this review and other one our blog:<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://southernbredsouthernread.blogspot.com/">http://southernbredsouthernread.blogs...</a><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://southernbredsouthernread.blogspot.com/">http://southernbredsouthernread.blogs...</a><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://southernbredsouthernread.blogspot.com/">http://southernbredsouthernread.blogs...</a></span>

<div id="review_1342919022" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1342919022" />
    <a title="Olivia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31987237-olivia"><img alt="Olivia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1485903861p2/31987237.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1342919022?book_show_action=true">Jul 23, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Olivia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Olivia" href="/user/show/31987237-olivia">Olivia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31987237-olivia?shelf=2015">2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1342919022" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2422426941044813609">Actual rating: 3.75/5<br/><br/>This is an excerpt from my review of the whole Shatter Me series. Read the full review here: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://bibliomad.wordpress.com/2015/07/22/shatter-me-series-by-tahereh-mafi-book-review/'>https://bibliomad.wordpress.com/2015/...</a><br/><br/>This is not your average book series. This doesn’t even come close to your average book series. Think The Hunger Games but with more metaphors. Think Divergent but with more heart. Even then, even then, you are not even close. This is the Shatter Me series, and words don’t come close to describing how I feel about it. Whenever I think about thi</span>
  <span id="freeText2422426941044813609" style="display:none">Actual rating: 3.75/5<br /><br />This is an excerpt from my review of the whole Shatter Me series. Read the full review here: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://bibliomad.wordpress.com/2015/07/22/shatter-me-series-by-tahereh-mafi-book-review/">https://bibliomad.wordpress.com/2015/...</a><br /><br />This is not your average book series. This doesn’t even come close to your average book series. Think The Hunger Games but with more metaphors. Think Divergent but with more heart. Even then, even then, you are not even close. This is the Shatter Me series, and words don’t come close to describing how I feel about it. Whenever I think about this series I want to scream. Out of joy, out of frustration, out of typical fangirl tendencies.<br /><br />I heard about this series through Goodreads, and the reviews pinned it to be so utterly flawless that I had very high hopes. And, overall, I was not disappointed.<br /><br />Tahereh Mafi writes poetically and lyrically. Her words interlock so perfectly, it’s as if they were destined to be written side by side. This injects a rhythm into her books, which I believe this genre is lacking. Every other sentence is interlaced with a metaphor, and in using this method, Mafi’s ideas and Juliette’s emotions come across much more prominently than if she had used plain words.<br /><br />Furthermore, Mafi writes in a way that gives you an insight into the mind of this girl – Juliette – who is clearly very crazed due to her time in solidarity. The constant use of repetition, as if Juliette has to repeat herself so as to get through to herself. The crossing out of words, as if Juliette is crossing out thoughts, trying not to think certain things, or simply crossing things out on a page. The long flowing sentences, like Juliette’s never-ending thoughts. The short, powerful sentences, depicting sudden changes in her emotion. It’s this craft that makes this series what it is. Without it, it would not be so highly praised.<br /><br />The storyline is not pristine. There are many flaws, and many reasons to believe Mafi simply wanted to write a love story, but more on that later.<br /><br />Overall, this series is magnificent, and truly one of a kind. I look forward to reading more from Mafi in the future, for she is destined to be a big hit in the YA community.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2422426941044813609" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1725466623" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1725466623" />
    <a title="Jynt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5812701-jynt"><img alt="Jynt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1371397197p2/5812701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1725466623?book_show_action=true">Aug 11, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jynt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jynt" href="/user/show/5812701-jynt">Jynt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5812701-jynt?shelf=the-3s-and-4s">the-3s-and-4s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5812701-jynt?shelf=ya-surprise">ya-surprise</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1725466623&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1725466623" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16353142412692006247">Honestly enjoyed this. I did think Adam went through some unnecessary butchering to get the relationships in place, but I'm quite pleased where it ended up (because I'm a fangirl at heart). Speaking of relationships, I thought it was a tad dramatic, but then you had Kenji and his comments poking fun at the drama. That was a nice touch - it showed self-awareness, and ensured that I never felt that this book took itself too seriously. <br/><br/>Plot wise, there was nothing overly surprising. In a sense, I g</span>
  <span id="freeText16353142412692006247" style="display:none">Honestly enjoyed this. I did think Adam went through some unnecessary butchering to get the relationships in place, but I'm quite pleased where it ended up (because I'm a fangirl at heart). Speaking of relationships, I thought it was a tad dramatic, but then you had Kenji and his comments poking fun at the drama. That was a nice touch - it showed self-awareness, and ensured that I never felt that this book took itself too seriously. <br /><br />Plot wise, there was nothing overly surprising. In a sense, I guess you could say this was a very formulaic story - though it just goes to show that formulas do work eh? <br /><br />Writing was interesting - the first two books had an odd style which I think was done on purpose to emphasize Juliette's mental instability - she is the narrator after all. By the third book, that was mostly gone, signalling her return to normalcy. <br /><br />I'm a bit displeased with the ending though - loads of loose ends. Can I hope there may be more? Probably not since the author's note signaled quite a definitive end - for Juliette's story anyway. Ah well. Nothing is wrapped up neatly in life, anyway. <br /><br />Side books showcasing events from male leads POV was quite a nice too. Although I must say I enjoyed Warner's one more than Adam's - simply because of my fangirl leanings. Hur. What can I say? I like the bad/misunderstood angsty trope. <br /><br />Overall, one of the better entries in YA? I mean, it doesn't break any new ground, but it is populated with characters you can care for, with all the necessary growth and plot movement too. Easy to read if you're just looking for some brain candy. If you're looking for something more than a love triangle and a predictable story trajectory... this may not be it. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16353142412692006247" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1034958043" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1034958043" />
    <a title="Simra ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34250169-simra"><img alt="Simra ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408849451p2/34250169.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1034958043?book_show_action=true">Aug 23, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Simra ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Simra ♥" href="/user/show/34250169-simra">Simra ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1034958043" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13151287037359289378">When I first saw "Shatter Me" on Goodreads as I was looking for books to read, I didn't think much of it because of the tremendous amount of bad ratings the first book had. My friend persuaded me to give it a try anyway, saying that the series got better as the books went on. And so I did, and I will never regret my decision. I finished this series in about a week and a half - which I honestly think isn't too bad. What makes this series so unforgettable is Mafi's deception of Juliette's (the mai</span>
  <span id="freeText13151287037359289378" style="display:none">When I first saw "Shatter Me" on Goodreads as I was looking for books to read, I didn't think much of it because of the tremendous amount of bad ratings the first book had. My friend persuaded me to give it a try anyway, saying that the series got better as the books went on. And so I did, and I will never regret my decision. I finished this series in about a week and a half - which I honestly think isn't too bad. What makes this series so unforgettable is Mafi's deception of Juliette's (the main character) voice. It's utterly captivating. Throughout the books, you see this broken girl who hates herself for who she is grow into a strong and confident woman. If you pick up this series with the mindset that there will be a lot of worldbuilding, you should walk away right now - because there isn't. The main focus is on the characters and their growth - there is /a lot/ of character development, and romance that will have your head spinning and wanting more. There will be characters that will frustrate you, characters that will amuse you, and characters that you will fall deeply in love with. The metaphors and analogies used in this series are absolutely beautiful - Mafi truly does have a way with words. Her writing style is unique - it may not be for everyone, but I personally enjoyed it. If you're looking for a quick series to read this month; one that will make you laugh and cry and beg for more, then Shatter Me is for you. <br /><br />Note: Book 1.5 and Book 2.5 are both novellas - told in two different characters' POV's (not Juliette's). I'd highly recommend reading them also, or you'll miss out on a lot.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13151287037359289378" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3095168323572385603">Just finished this.<br/><br/>I think while the writing and the prose do not impress me (not going to be highlighting quotes from this series), character development was fantastic. I like how every character is given a distinct personality. I spy some Kenji fans in the comment section. He definitely provided some comedic relief and cute little James. I was just reading this as an easy read. The kind of book with light contents, not really fussy, don't have to crack your brain juice kinda book. And it was l</span>
  <span id="freeText3095168323572385603" style="display:none">Just finished this.<br /><br />I think while the writing and the prose do not impress me (not going to be highlighting quotes from this series), character development was fantastic. I like how every character is given a distinct personality. I spy some Kenji fans in the comment section. He definitely provided some comedic relief and cute little James. I was just reading this as an easy read. The kind of book with light contents, not really fussy, don't have to crack your brain juice kinda book. And it was like that for the first two books. Boring Adam, droning Juliette, and the occasional Kenji jokes. But the novella with Warner perspective, that blew me away and in the third book, when Warner's actions were unravelled (Ah! I see what Taherah did there!), I was in love. I see a lot of people commenting on Chapter 55. I am not too big of a fan there, it is nice to see them get together and Warner being happy, but the redeeming moments for me were the ones of Warner simply being intensely in love, self conscious of his scars, his tough boy act, fiercely protective, and clean. I like clean boys. I loved the part where he came to her when she pressed on her pager and he just swooped her into his arms and wanted to do anything for her. The fact that he could feel her pain, that was..intense. I also liked the little soap talk they had and him swooping her into the bathroom. Yeah, I am a sucker. So while my literary love object was Peeta from the Hunger Games series, I guess Warner is taking his place for now. Yet another series where I end up reading it for the side characters rather than the main. <br /><br />God Warner, you are perfect. <br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4964532042203092173">Imagine a youthful life in which your touch was actually deadly. What if one of your memories included the horrific death of a little boy whom you killed when your intent was simply to help him stand after a fall in a grocery store. That death, and a host of similar problems, caused your parents to turn against you, and you ultimately are incarcerated in an assylum for the criminally insane. You are allowed no human contact and for nearly a year, your only entertainment is a notebook you are kee</span>
  <span id="freeText4964532042203092173" style="display:none">Imagine a youthful life in which your touch was actually deadly. What if one of your memories included the horrific death of a little boy whom you killed when your intent was simply to help him stand after a fall in a grocery store. That death, and a host of similar problems, caused your parents to turn against you, and you ultimately are incarcerated in an assylum for the criminally insane. You are allowed no human contact and for nearly a year, your only entertainment is a notebook you are keeping for your benefit. So dreadful is your isolation, you fear that perhaps you actually are dead. <br /><br />Then into your life and cell comes a young man who treats you kindly, and miraculously enough, does not wither when you touch him. Such is the case for young Juliette, a 17-year-old who must learn to harness the seemingly horrific power she has and use that power to liberate a despotic world.<br /><br />I mostly enjoyed this series. It gets three stars because I was never able to make the transition Juliette had to make when her love interest changes in the series. So believable is ∫ young man Adam as a kind loving man that a change in the final portion of the series seemed difficult to make for me. <br /><br />I enjoyed the author's unique and compelling writing style, however, and I'd definitely read other books she creates. </span>

<div id="review_988310425" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/988310425" />
    <a title="Melanie Jacobson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/427927-melanie-jacobson"><img alt="Melanie Jacobson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557160531p2/427927.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/988310425?book_show_action=true">Jul 06, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie Jacobson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie Jacobson" href="/user/show/427927-melanie-jacobson">Melanie Jacobson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer988310425" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13037906507426846437">So, on the plus side, this trilogy came highly recommended from several sources, and I'll continue to trust them. I don't finish many trilogies (there has to be something truly special going on for me to want to go through three books with the same character when you can pretty much guess the ending) and I finished this one in a week. IT's mainly the author's voice; her use of figurative language, the strike throughs, the raw emotion of the storytelling, the intensive relationship between Juliet</span>
  <span id="freeText13037906507426846437" style="display:none">So, on the plus side, this trilogy came highly recommended from several sources, and I'll continue to trust them. I don't finish many trilogies (there has to be something truly special going on for me to want to go through three books with the same character when you can pretty much guess the ending) and I finished this one in a week. IT's mainly the author's voice; her use of figurative language, the strike throughs, the raw emotion of the storytelling, the intensive relationship between Juliette and her guys--all very compelling reasons to read on. Also, Kenji, and his friendship with Juliette, is pretty much the best. On the down side, Juliette often got on may last nerve. There were a few times where I almost put the book down because her self-absorption was so irritating, only to find in the very next chapter that she'd have an important self-realization. Too many times that took too long though. Also, the sensuality is pretty out there. No way I'd put this in the hands of my teens. Ditto the language on every page. (Didn't read 1.5 and 2.5, just 1, 2, and 3).</span>
  <a data-text-id="13037906507426846437" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText6007809950493622148" style="display:none">A fascinating read. Mafi’s writing is almost visceral at times. She drags you into her world and her emotive writing style keep your eyes transfixed to the page. It feels like you’re on a runaway high speed train charging off to an amazing climax. This is I think my only qualm with the series that I find the endings of Mafi’s books rather sedate in comparison. In part this is due to the first person account, and our main character is somehow often whisked away from the very climactic battles you have been anticipating. Thus the big battles are compressed into accounts to the main character in the subsequent book. To me it feels as if someone has pulled the emergency brake on this amazing train ride. I was really worried when finishing ‘Ignite Me’ that there was still supposed to be an extra book to follow the series which I wasn’t aware of to conclude the series properly. I was very near to the end and there were still many story lines that needed coming together. It felt somewhat rushed, perhaps due to my desire to remain in her world…</span>

<div id="review_3288332656" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3288332656" />
    <a title="Steff Pasciuti" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10337759-steff-pasciuti"><img alt="Steff Pasciuti" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600380747p2/10337759.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3288332656?book_show_action=true">Apr 18, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steff Pasciuti" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steff Pasciuti" href="/user/show/10337759-steff-pasciuti">Steff Pasciuti</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10337759-steff-pasciuti?shelf=super-problematic">super-problematic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10337759-steff-pasciuti?shelf=kill-it-with-fire">kill-it-with-fire</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10337759-steff-pasciuti?shelf=cringe">cringe</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10337759-steff-pasciuti?shelf=abuse-romanticzing-trash">abuse-romanticzing-trash</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10337759-steff-pasciuti?shelf=hate-the-mc">hate-the-mc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10337759-steff-pasciuti?shelf=sensitive-topics">sensitive-topics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3288332656" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10936747963713299718">The Shatter Me series romanticizes abuse; <a href='https://spasciuti.com/abuse-in-novels/' rel='nofollow noopener'>click here</a> for an ongoing, in-depth commentary about abuse romanticism in this series and others.<br/><br/>| <a href='https://spasciuti.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>Reader Fox Blog</a> | <br/><a href='https://spasciuti.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1586415338i/29258676.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>It must have been over a year ago now that I said I was going to be rereading the <em>Shatter Me </em>series in order to shed some light on the deeply problematic aspects of abuse romanticism that exists within the series. Well, I'd started but eventually lost track due to life and my desire to read books that were more deserving of my attentio</span>
  <span id="freeText10936747963713299718" style="display:none">The Shatter Me series romanticizes abuse; <a href="https://spasciuti.com/abuse-in-novels/" rel="nofollow noopener">click here</a> for an ongoing, in-depth commentary about abuse romanticism in this series and others.<br><br>| <a href="https://spasciuti.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Reader Fox Blog</a> | <br><a href="https://spasciuti.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1586415338i/29258676.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>It must have been over a year ago now that I said I was going to be rereading the <em>Shatter Me </em>series in order to shed some light on the deeply problematic aspects of abuse romanticism that exists within the series. Well, I'd started but eventually lost track due to life and my desire to read books that were more deserving of my attention.<br><br> Last night I finally started. <br><br>I ordered physical copies of the first three books and the short stories that exist in between them. I opened <em>Shatter Me </em>last night and began. As of this moment, I have only annotated the first nine and a half chapters. It's interesting, reading this book again. I had enjoyed it the first time. Never in my life had I expected that the author would try to manipulate me into liking the despicable Warner.<br><br>Forgiveness is important in life, for sure, but I don't think it plays a role here. There are some things that are unforgivable. And honestly? If Warner genuinely wanted to develop himself and become a better person, it should have been with someone else. To have Juliette degrade herself and regress entirely in her character development to the point that she falls for her abuser was disturbing on a number of insane levels.<br><br>Warner's obsession with Juliette is terrifying. And I haven't even truly scratched the surface yet.<br><br>I am <em>baffled</em> by the fact that people find their relationship romantic. I am deeply saddened by the fact that "broken" characters somehow are given the okay to horrifically damage their partners in the name of love. As if the fact that they love this person makes it okay that they hurt them in these ways.<br><br>It doesn't make it okay. He did not deserve or earn her forgiveness. And once I've finished annotating all of these books, I will share with you all why that is.<br><br>To any girl who meets a boy who was "broken" by the way someone in his life treated him, who gets treated horribly by this boy -- run. His brokenness does not make it okay for him to hurt you. His brokenness does not mean that he deserves your forgiveness. There are plenty of people who suffer abuse and do not lash out and abuse the people they "love."<br><br>Mafi manipulates her readers to try and force them to like Warner. She creates characters and then manipulates them into unrealistic actions in order to push them in the direction she wanted, even if it doesn't actually make any sense to do so. In this way, I see these books as being very poorly written.<br><br>But the worst thing of all is the fact that abuse is lauded as romantic in these novels. Warner may hurt Juliette and be forgiven for it time and time again all because, beneath his terrible acts, his motives are <em>supposedly</em> based in the fact that he loves her. Nevermind that time and time again his <em>love</em> is portrayed as selfish and only insofar as she benefits him.<br><br>Like the novels, if you wish. But at least like them knowing the facts: Warner is abusive. Juliette and Warner are in an abusive relationship.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1587252051i/29316891.jpg" alt="" width="348" height="372" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>| <a href="https://www.instagram.com/spasciuti/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://mobile.twitter.com/SPasciuti_" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://spasciuti.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Reader Fox Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/@spasciuti" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a> | <a href="https://m.facebook.com/SteffPasciutiReaderFox/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> |</span>
  <a data-text-id="10936747963713299718" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2330030910" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2330030910" />
    <a title="Michele Evans" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20793887-michele-evans"><img alt="Michele Evans" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1440477994p2/20793887.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer8620628459941409915">I absolutely loved this series. It was a mix of post-apocalyptic, dystopian, super human, romance and many others.<br/><br/>Juliette Ferrars has a curse, or a gift, depending on which way you look at it. Her touch can render another person immobile and kill them. Always ridiculed and talked abo</span>
  <span id="freeText8620628459941409915" style="display:none">I absolutely loved this series. It was a mix of post-apocalyptic, dystopian, super human, romance and many others.<br /><br />Juliette Ferrars has a curse, or a gift, depending on which way you look at it. Her touch can render another person immobile and kill them. She has been in a psychiatric ward for just under a year, after being rejected for years by her family, her classmates, her community, and has spent the majority of her adolescence locked up in one form or another. Always ridiculed and talked about, treated like the walking plague, she never wanted anything but the things others take for granted - the ability to hold someone’s hand, the loving hugs from a caring parent, someone who would be her friend. But up until this story starts, she has experienced none of this.<br /><br />Living in a world that has been torn apart by war and the detrimental state of our planet, the Reestablishment has vowed to take care of everyone’s worries, turn the planet back to a place of beauty, and be the people’s salvation. The only problem is with all their promises being nothing but pretty lies, they have enslaved the entire population across the globe, where the only ones benefitting from their dictatorship are the highest leaders of the organization. They live among riches and eat extravagantly, while everyone else slaves to acquire food for their families, on the verge of starvation, if not already lost to it. Everyone has experienced loss at the hands of this new order, yet it has grown in size so fast that nobody can stand against them.<br /><br />Juliette is broken out of the insane insylum, only to become a prisoner of the Reestablishment and told she will become their weapon.<br /><br />I do not wish to give away individual books details but this story was amazing from book one to the last one, and all the smaller novellas in between. I lost sleep at night because I didn’t want to quit reading- I had to know what would happen next! Definitely put the next book on my wishlist- can’t wait to hear what’s next!<br /><br />This author is super amazing and incredibly gifted!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="8620628459941409915" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="Jessica Pietro" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26901214-jessica-pietro"><img alt="Jessica Pietro" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588935348p2/26901214.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3215368870?book_show_action=true">Aug 03, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica Pietro" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica Pietro" href="/user/show/26901214-jessica-pietro">Jessica Pietro</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26901214-jessica-pietro?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3215368870" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14073295609244532171">(reviewing the whole series)<br/><br/>I LOVED THIS SERIES! I have many underlines throughout each of the books and definitely plan to read them again in the future. I have already read them twice.<br/><br/>This series kept me on my toes the whole time. There were so many twists and unexpected turns! The romance was amazing, especially after book 1. The vivid imagery of the emotions in the main character were so intense. I was truly feeling all of her emotions as I read. Especially the internal struggle which was ex</span>
  <span id="freeText14073295609244532171" style="display:none">(reviewing the whole series)<br /><br />I LOVED THIS SERIES! I have many underlines throughout each of the books and definitely plan to read them again in the future. I have already read them twice.<br /><br />This series kept me on my toes the whole time. There were so many twists and unexpected turns! The romance was amazing, especially after book 1. The vivid imagery of the emotions in the main character were so intense. I was truly feeling all of her emotions as I read. Especially the internal struggle which was expressed by the lines that were crossed out. There was a wide cast of characters but only a few were majorly focused on which I liked. Sometimes books go into too much detail with too many people and it can be tiring to keep up with. Throughout the series you get to experience multiple points of view which is something I really love to see also! It's nice to experience different perspectives and get a break from the more exhausting emotional characters while inside the head of a snarky and humorous one.<br /><br />I have heard some people say the series should have ended sooner than it did but I disagree. Not only would the story itself have been incomplete, but the characters would not have been able to develop and evolve to the extent they did if it had ended as a trilogy. I am happy to have traveled with these characters for longer, getting to know the core group of side characters just as deeply as the actual lead female character, and especially, watching one particular character transform and grow. (No spoilers!!)<br /><br />I highly recommend this series! 5 stars!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14073295609244532171" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Delightful.<br/><br/>‘Unravel me’ pathetically continues the former by hyper focusing on an awkward, not well-developed love triangle with overly detailed make out scenes. The writer fails to maintain the captivating writing style and leaves the characters lifeless. Dissatisfying.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('++t+DAGN7rx2CKZXwATdaYpFu6Mypkmv5uLhCWi/yAvwAwH6hKxQwG3lMDfE0vfvnZwXxu7E1/J47EWUDwPdPg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

But the Kingdom needs only one huntress to save it, and what it takes could tear Kaede and Taisin apart forever.\n\nThe exciting adventure prequel to Malinda Lo\'s highly acclaimed novel Ash is overflowing with lush Chinese influences and details inspired by the I Ching, and is filled with action and romance.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"6069028432886923889\" href=\"#\"   <span id="freeText11805585972918555013" style="display:none">Tahereh Mafi is the <i>New York Times</i> and <i>USA Today</i> bestselling author of the <i>Shatter Me</i> series. She was born in a small city somewhere in Connecticut and currently resides in Santa Monica, California with her husband, fellow author <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3046613.Ransom_Riggs" title="Ransom Riggs" rel="nofollow noopener">Ransom Riggs</a>. She can usually be found over-caffeinated and stuck in a book. <i>Shatter Me</i> is her first series, with television rights optioned by ABC Signature Studios; <i>Furthermore</i>, her first middle grade novel, is on shelves now, and <i>Whichwood</i>, its darker companion, will be on shelves November 14, 2017.</span>
